< Text>
WOODLAND GAMESTOP: I live in Marysville, but come to Woodland 1-2 times per week on business, and since I love gaming, I have frequented GameStop. I am a card carring member and have purchased multiple platforms for both myself and family members as gifts, I've purchased new and used games, and am familiar with trading, as well. I had purchased a game for my XBox One that was suppose to play on it--according to the clerk. It was a 360 game, but was assured it was compatible. I took it home and it was several days until I got a chance to open it and try it out. Nope. It didn't work. I then went to the internet to check out the particular game for myself. It, too, said, no go. So, the following week, I called the Woodland GameStop, told them about the problem, and I was assured that I could bring the item back for a full refund. A week went by, and I finally  got to Woodland with the game and receipt. The clerk looked at the item and said he couldn't accept the item for return as it had been opened. I explained that I had been assured it was compatible, when it wasn't. He said he was sorry, but that was store policy. I went around and around with him again a few times relating the whole story with many customers watching in amazement as both he and I  got a little louder.  I asked to talk to his manager, and he said he was the manager. Whether he was or not, I do not know. At my rope's end I finally asked if I could at least get store credit for the game and he yelled back at me he wouldn't do that either, that he had done everything he could for me, and that because of store policy, he could do no more. He kept saying that. Store policy wouldn't allow him to do anything. The following week I went to a GameStop in Yuba City, and what a different story, I got there. At once, the clerk told me that I never should have been assured that game was compatible because there is a list the clerk could have easily checked. Second, I was overcharged. Third, I didn't get the credits on my card. Fourth, this clerk was polite and willing to help me where the Woodland GameStop clerk wouldn't. So, I know that the only policy was that the Woodland store made up there own police and customer relations were not important to them. I will never shop at that store again. I continue to be a member of GameStop, but now I am loyal to the Yuba City store. It seems to me that as long as they are taking your money they are happy with you, but as soon as there is a problem, watch out, you don't know how they will treat you.</Text>

< Text>
TL;DR: On the pricey side, mediocre rolls, subpar cleanliness.

Went in during lunch rush and ordered three rolls to share with my significant other. Water that was brought to us had lots of dried water stains and felt dusty. The waitress informed that there would be a bit of a wait, as we ordered the special rolls. Wait was quite long, as we got our rolls around 10-15  minutes apart from each other. The fish tasted quite fresh, but the overall construction of the rolls were not as great.  Price for three of the rolls totaled to around $60, but I felt like the amount we got was not worth the price.</Text>

I have been going to Seven Seas when it was still Godzilla Sushi. So I have been a loyal customer for a number of years. I go there nearly everyday for lunch.
During my last visit I had placed my order. A few minutes later I had asked my server if I could change my order. In the past they have been good about doing that. This time the server added on to my original order.
I clarified that I wanted to cancel my original order. The server notified the chef and he said he was already making the sushi roll. So basically, I got stuck paying for everything because the chef was unwilling to accommodate my request.
Needless to say I was not only upset but highly disappointed. Seven Seas will be losing a very loyal customer because of their server's mistake and their unreasonable chef.
Next time I crave Japanese food I will just have to make a special trip to Japantown or walk a little farther away.< /Review>

Nice little restaurant. Bigger than it looks. The menu is quite large and selection of roll is good. They do carry interesting rolls. Rolls are overall on the large side. Did order a rice less roll and was really good. Quickly deep fried so the outside of the roll was cooked and the texture felt like rice. Service is fast and price are ok. They do offer food to go. We tried 4 rolls and one of them had a 1 chilly rating for spicineness so if you are sensitive to spicy food follow the rating I believe it is quite accurate. 1 chili hot but not burning. Fish was really good and no smell or strange taste. Overall a very good experience and will be back.</Text>

< review>
I rarely write post about places, especially bad post, unless I had a memorable moment there. And this place, well let's say I haven't had a hospital make me feel bad for being worried about my health. I went into the ER on July 17th with symptoms of a heart attack. Now I am 22 years old, so you can understand my fear of why I felt like I was about to have a heart attack. Plus, both my family (mother and father side) have heart problems and we are prone to heart attacks. I went in to make sure and mostly to have the pain go away. When I got in at first they were okay, acting friendly and all that. But then my assigned nurse came to meet me, his interaction with me was dismissive of my heart attack. Understandable I'm young but he wasn't even concerned to why I was having chest pains. I tried to explain to him my concern with my family's health history but each time I spoke he would dismiss it. It was like he had made up his mind about my health and heart. Anyway, they ran two test and then confirmed I wasn't having a heart attack. My nurse told me that I was cleared but he didn't tell me what the problem was. I was still in extreme pain as he pretty much told me to go home. I was trying to get an answer but he just said well it isn't a heart attack so you can go home. No one even thought of giving me an answer or pain medicine. I left feeling cruddy both physically and at this point mentally. I felt like I was an idiot for being concerned and that my health is not important to even medical professionals. I went home and just tried to move on with my day but by 9 pm I couldn't deal with it anymore. The pain was at an extreme high and I needed help. I went to a different hospital. Told the the exact same thing but instead of dismissing my concerns they tested me for everything the pain could be. Even for a heart attack!! The nurse at Regional treated me with kindness and he showed concern to my pain. He helped me out way more than my nurse at O'Connor. Regional was able to help minimize the pain so I could even go back to my daily activity.
I was very disappointed at the service I had here. I wouldn't have minded the dismissive attitude my assigned nurse had, if I was at least given something for the pain. Or at least had someone tell me what to do with the pain. I feel like my experience at O'Connor has really soured my feeling of trust and safety with them. I don't see myself coming back here except in dire need. Otherwise, I am going to Regional from now on. They at least will go the extra mile to find out what the pain actually is coming from.</review>

I did get snappy towards the end because she absolutely had no compassion and she basically told me I better watch the way I was speaking to her.  I didn't yell, swear or do anything of the sort. In n out pretty fast, and he even made a wrong diagnosis on me one time, luckily, my dental hygienist pointed out to him that I should not receive such treatment because of the nature of my tooth.  Then, my hygienist told me that's pretty basic stuff and she wondered why my dentist didn't recognize it.  My previous dentist is not paying attention, and that scares the heck out of me.  Now, I am with Dr. To, he is 40 miles away from my home, but that doesn't stop me from going because he is professional, caring, and he spends quality time with me and other patients (from what I observe).
